Original Text of the Judgment by the Jiangsu High Court in the Labor Dispute Case of the Sanyou Factory 122

Based on the revised Regulations for Handling Labor Disputes,

The employer cannot appeal against the arbitration decision.

The labor dispute at the Sanyou Industrial Society in Pudong, after being arbitrated by the municipal government, was appealed by the employer to the local court, which rejected the appeal. The employer still refused to accept the decision and appealed to the High Court, which, after hearing the case, also rejected the appeal. The original text of the judgment is excerpted below:

(Main Text) The appeal and incidental appeal, as well as the application for provisional execution, are all rejected. The costs of the second instance shall be borne by the appellant. (Facts omitted)

(Reasoning) The main purpose of the matters that the appellant declared should be adjudicated in this case is to seek confirmation that the employment contract has been terminated and, based on this reason, to request the annulment of the No. 20 arbitration decision made by the Shanghai Labor-Management Arbitration Committee on September 1 of this year (hereinafter referred to as the Committee Decision), and to order the appellee to return the occupied part of the factory and its equipment. Whether the employment contract has been terminated is indeed the central issue of the decision. According to the appellant, the Hongxianggang factory was suddenly attacked during the Shanghai Incident on January 28 of this year. The factory was occupied by enemy troops, the workers all left the factory long ago, and all work was completely stopped. The company paid off the remaining wages, implemented dissolution, and repeatedly posted notices in newspapers and reported to the relevant authorities for assistance. According to Article 30, Paragraph 2 of the Factory Law, the employment contract has indeed been terminated. This Court finds that both parties signed ten articles of treatment conditions on March 14, 1929, stipulating that if workers are dismissed or resign, they must be handled in accordance with Item 8 of the Provisional Measures for Retirement Treatment of Employees in Shanghai Special Municipality, as clearly stated in Article 5 of the conditions. The appellant did not follow the provisions of Article 5 of the negotiated measures, applying Item 8, and did not submit it to the Social Affairs Bureau for approval, but subjectively believed that the workers had been dismissed, which is not in accordance with the regulations. Regarding the appellant's claim that the treatment conditions signed by both parties at that time stated in the appendix that if the government amended the regulations in the future, the amended laws and regulations would still be followed and that the Factory Law should not be cited now, according to Article 30 of the Factory Law, if a factory suspends work for more than one month due to force majeure, it should still give prior notice in accordance with Article 27 of the same law. Although the reason for the suspension of work at the Hongxianggang factory this time was due to the suddenness of the war, a force majeure, it still cannot be considered that the obligation to give prior notice is waived according to law. Reviewing the appellant's notice on January 29, it only stated that the current situation was suddenly changing and extremely dangerous, and that all work in all departments was suspended. The announcements published in the newspapers on March 8 and May 24 also only stated that the factory was forced to suspend work due to its location, that the Japanese army was still stationed in the factory and had not yet withdrawn, and that the houses, machinery, and equipment were all beyond repair and could not be started. Do not mistakenly listen to rumors and make unnecessary trips. All of this indicated a suspension of work and did not declare closure and dismissal, so it cannot be regarded as a prior notice. According to current civil law, if the notice of termination is not received within the time limit, the right to terminate is extinguished (see Article 257 of the Civil Code). The appellant's strenuous arguments inevitably lead to stubborn prejudices. Since the employment contract has not been terminated, as stated above, except for the recent workers who voluntarily received wages from the appellant's company, wrote letters of intent, and sought other livelihoods, the rest are still in the company waiting for work after the incident is resolved. Living in the original factory houses cannot be called occupation, so there is no requirement for prosecution and return. The Shanghai Municipal Government, seeing that both parties had exhausted their means and could not resolve the situation themselves, accepted the parties' petitions and handled the matter. If the handling failed, the Labor-Management Arbitration Committee was organized to make a decision according to law. This was originally to protect the interests of both labor and management and to achieve peace and tranquility, and it was a power granted by current laws and regulations. Although the appellant vehemently stated the pros and cons of the Committee Decision, believing that it could not be followed, the main points were nothing more than that partial resumption of work was impossible, that dismissed workers should be employed by the Hangzhou factory first, that there were practical obstacles, and that there were concerns that disputes would arise over retirement pay. However, the loss of the Hongxiang factory due to the incident is a fact, but the Sanyou Industrial Society has not closed down due to the Shanghai Incident. The company still has more than two million yuan in capital, and the committee designated Accountant Pan to check the accounts. The results showed that the actual losses in recent years have not reached 200,000 yuan, and the capital stock has been depleted by only less than 10%. In terms of financial resources, restoring the Hongxianggang factory is not absolutely impossible. Reducing the scale, adapting to the circumstances, reconfiguring, and resuming part of the work, what is impossible? Although the harvest may be small, wages and various expenses can be reduced together. Weighing the pros and cons, it is not impossible to maintain. As for the workers who should resume work, the criteria for selecting people should be determined by the labor union itself. The decision did not order the appellant to choose, so there is no need to worry too much. If the Hangzhou Municipal Government prohibits the dismissal of workers, making it difficult to implement at that time, the appellant may request the relevant administrative authorities to seek other remedies. Moreover, since the appellant promised the Shanghai Municipal Government that it would find another way to proceed in the nearby Hangzhou factory and seek to expand it at any time in order to reduce the number of unemployed workers, it has now suddenly gone back on its word, claiming that it is impossible in fact, which is obviously an excuse for shirking responsibility. Whether retirement pay should be enjoyed after dismissal is also clearly stipulated by laws and regulations, which can be handled easily and should not be asserted as a matter of litigation. The original trial court found that the appellant's request was not justified and rejected the appellant's lawsuit, which was not inappropriate. Furthermore, the Regulations for Handling Labor Disputes have been revised and promulgated on September 27 of this year. Article 7, Paragraph 1 of the law states that the disputing party may not appeal against the decision of the arbitration committee. Article 44, Paragraph 2 stipulates that disputes that occurred before the promulgation and implementation of the revised law and have not yet been resolved may be handled in accordance with this law. Although this case has been decided by the arbitration committee, the lawsuit has not yet ended, that is, the dispute has not yet been resolved. The appellant has no reason to object to the arbitration decision. Furthermore, although the employment contracts of the appellees have not been legally terminated, the appellant's factory was indeed suspended due to an event of force majeure, and it did not fail to pay wages on time without reason, so it is not liable for compensation. Since there is no obligation to compensate, there is no need to declare provisional execution. It goes without saying that the original trial court also rejected the appellee's counterclaim and application for provisional execution, which was also not inappropriate. Based on the above conclusions, the appeal and incidental appeal in this case are both without merit. In accordance with Article 415 and Article 81 of the Civil Procedure Law, the judgment is as stated in the main text. Jiangsu High Court, Second Civil Division. Presiding Judge Wu Yuxin. 印. Judge Lu Wen 印. Judge Chen Kui 印.

Mrs. Macchison's Coffin was Sealed Yesterday

Mr. Macchison's Condition Remained Unchanged Yesterday 123

After the crash of Soong Tse-vung's privately owned plane, the Sikorsky, the condition of the injured pilot, Mr. Macchison, has not changed. His wife, Mrs. Philip, was placed in a coffin at 3:30 p.m. yesterday at the International Funeral Parlor on Jiaozhou Road. She will soon be transported back to her hometown of Philadelphia, USA, for burial.

The Electricity Company Again Attempts to Threaten Users by Cutting Off Power

Taxpayers Association Sends Letter to the Municipal Council Requesting Correction 125

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Chief Secretary of the Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "To the esteemed Chief Secretary, according to a letter from Zheng Xinji of Jin Business Bureau, our bureau is located at No. 765 East Agulu Road. The electricity is under the name of Zheng Xinji, which has been used for about ten years. Regarding electricity bills, we have always paid them in full according to the bills from the Municipal Council's Electrical Department and now the Shanghai Electric Power Company. The recording, inspection, installation, and removal of electricity meters have never been notified or consulted with us, nor is there any way to consult. Unexpectedly, on January 6th of this year at 12:00 AM, we received a letter from the Shanghai Electric Power Company dated January 5th, stating that the motor meter was inspected as usual on December 1st of last year, and it was found that the hard seal was forged. The electric light meter was inspected on December 14th, and the old meter was removed on the 15th. After testing in the laboratory, it was found that the magnet inside was displaced and the speed was reduced by 29.5%. We must pay a supplementary electricity fee of 122 taels, 8 qian, and 8 fen from January 15, 1929, to December 15, 1932, within 48 hours, otherwise, the power supply will be cut off. The bill has been sent. To determine a crime, first, there must be strong evidence, and this evidence must be acknowledged by the person involved and certified by a notary. Second, there must be a final judgment by the court. Now, the Shanghai Electric Power Company's evidence collection procedure is already non-compliant, and without a court trial and determination, it is both slander and a violation of the law. As for the supplementary fee from January 15, 1929, the company has self-determined the so-called forged hard seal from that date. What are the duties of the company's inspectors? Their arbitrariness is obvious. Furthermore, the old meter was removed on December 15th of last year, and the situation was tested in the laboratory. Is this any different from a private individual determining in their home that the company's meter readers, inspectors, removers, and installers are all opportunists, demanding the company to compensate for losses? Our bureau, for the sake of justice and legal interests, is willing to let the company cut off power, causing our bureau to suffer illegal infringement and suspension of business, rather than pay this kind of money for which there is absolutely no legal obligation to pay, under the circumstances of the so-called findings in the company's laboratory before the company gets on the right legal track. However, if we allow the company's unfair enrichment method to succeed, there will be the following consequences: 'Under the company's self-assertion, (1) electricity users must pay fees without using electricity, (2) the electricity company can collect fees without supplying electricity, and the status of electricity users is in danger.' Your association is an organization to protect citizens. Even if it is not for the current situation of our bureau, it should consider the future of the citizens and seriously negotiate with the Municipal Council to stop the company's illegal schemes to seek unfair enrichment. The citizens will be fortunate, and our bureau will be fortunate." Upon receiving the letter, it was found that the actions of the Shanghai Electric Power Company are inconsistent with legal regulations. Previously, this was applied to Laoyan Maoyuan in Central City on Fuzhou Road, and we have repeatedly sent letters to your bureau requesting correction. Now, based on the previous situation, we hereby send a letter to your bureau requesting a swift correction to prevent the company from going its own way, causing all electricity users to be disheartened. Sincerely, Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council Chief Secretary.

Bloodshed at the Sincere Amusement Park 126

A Tourist's Sleeves Are Stained with Blood

Suspected and Arrested

Yesterday afternoon at 4:45 PM, a bloody assassination occurred inside the Dajing Class Theater at the Sincere Amusement Park on Nanjing Road. The victim was a middle-aged man, about thirty years old, whose name could not be found. The man was wearing a black faux-fur camel绒长袍, lined with a blue-threaded spring padded jacket and trousers. There were only two small yuan in his pocket. He was struck once in the face with an axe, twice in the back of the head, and had five or six wounds on both hands. Blood was all over the ground, and he had already died. The body was lying at the entrance between the sets of the Dajing Class Theater. The time of the murder and the identity of the murderer were unknown. Later, the park's staff discovered it and immediately reported it to the Laozha Police Station, which dispatched a large number of detectives to the scene to search for the murderer. As a result, they discovered a tourist-like person with bloodstains on his sleeves. When questioned, he was evasive and quite suspicious, so they took him to the police station for questioning. However, the man firmly denied committing the murder. As for his name, the police station is temporarily not announcing it because they still need to pursue accomplices. However, it is known that this person is from Shandong and is about forty years old. He is currently being held in the police station, while an investigation is underway to find the victim's family. The body was sent to Renji Hospital by Chinese patrol car No. 1565 and then transferred to the Philen Road Forensic Examination Office, pending a report to the court for examination this morning.

Over Four Hundred Inmates at the Local Court Detention Center Create a Major Commotion 127

| New Superintendent's Reforms Not Implemented |

| Detainees Feel Mistreated, Nearly Leading to a Major Incident |

All the detainees held in the Shanghai Local Court Detention Center are defendants whose cases have not yet been decided. In the past, all superintendents have followed the regulations of the Criminal Procedure Law, which allow defendants to provide their own food and daily necessities. Every morning, defendants could prepare their own breakfast snacks and receive money from family members for their use. Defendants whose cases have not been decided are treated differently from prisoners in jail. Former Superintendent Shao Zhenji's reform of exchanging cash gifts from family members for money vouchers caused inconvenience for defendants in their use and redemption, leading to complaints. After former Superintendent Shao was dismissed, newly appointed Superintendent Wang Tingqi took office. Superintendent Wang believed that there was a risk of corruption among the lower-level staff and clerks in the detention center, so he replaced all the old staff and changed all the facilities. For all visits with detainees, money given by family members was stored by the superintendent. If a defendant needed to provide their own food, they had to apply to the superintendent for approval one day in advance, who would then discretionarily allocate money for their use. Purchasing breakfast from outside was prohibited due to concerns about potential abuses. As a result, the more than four hundred detainees felt mistreated and collectively went on a hunger strike and created a commotion at 11:00 AM yesterday during mealtime. A major disaster was nearly averted in the detention center. Upon hearing the noise, Superintendent Wang immediately supervised the guards with guns to maintain order and reported to the court president and the chief prosecutor, who sent personnel to the detention center to investigate. He tried his best to persuade the defendants to accept improvements to their treatment within the bounds of the law. The inmates finally lowered their heads in obedience, became quiet, and returned to their original state. All the new policies of reform and innovation were then suspended. However, he had already had a good scare. The detention center's main gate was closed for an hour.

Brawl at Huaiyang Teahouse on Hengfeng Road 128

Bodyguards Participate Due to Misunderstanding

Guns and Bullets Fly, Police Arrive and Make Arrests

At 10:00 PM the night before last, dozens of hooligans suddenly appeared in front of the Huaiyang Teahouse at the intersection of Hengfeng Road in Zhabei, each inviting members of the bodyguard corps, and they mutually engaged in a group brawl. Both sides fired more than a dozen shots, fortunately without injuring anyone. The local Fourth District Second Precinct was notified, and Officers Yuan and Lin led the entire police force to suppress the situation, arresting more than ten defendants and plaintiffs on the spot and confiscating two six-inch handguns containing twenty-two bullets, as well as a car, all of which were taken to the station. The details are as follows:

Originating from a Female Worker's Suspension: Wang Agen, a 30-year-old man from Yancheng residing at No. 67 Hanzhong Road, is a foreman. His wife, Chen, used to work in a silk factory but was recently suspended by Chen Shiying, who was in charge of the machines, causing Wang to harbor resentment and constantly think about revenge. The night before last, he gathered members of the First Team of the Bodyguard Corps, Zhao Lianfa, Li Jinzhong, Li Fucheng, Dan Wufeng, and more than twenty hooligans, waiting at the Huaiyang Teahouse. Then, he borrowed a car with a concession pass number 6573 from his friend Gu Shenglin at No. 6 Baokang Lane, whose owner was a friend, and drove to Chen Shiying's house at No. 55 Changle Lane, intending to force Chen onto the car and bring him to the Huaiyang Teahouse to "drink tea" (mediate).

Chen to Arrive in Five Minutes: At the time, Chen Shiying was about to go out to visit friends when he caught sight of Wang loitering on the way, looking very nervous, fearing it would be detrimental to him. Therefore, he secretly invited his friends Xiao Wenbin and Jin Xianglin, who were members of the Eighth Team of the Bodyguard Corps, and more than ten workers to come out with him. Wang saw Chen and his group of people and found it inconvenient to act, so he stepped forward and said to Chen, "Please come to the Huaiyang Teahouse for a chat." Chen replied that he would arrive in five minutes. Wang then got into the car and waited at the teahouse.

A Chaotic Fight and Scuffle: After a while, Chen indeed went to the teahouse with more than ten people. Wang immediately instigated his assistants to grab Chen and beat him severely. At this time, Chen's friends stepped forward to fight back, and a chaotic fight ensued. Tables and chairs were overturned, and cups and pots flew everywhere. Soon, both sides opened fire, the gunshots sounding like a continuous string of pearls. The owner of the teahouse, fearing a major disaster, immediately called the Fourth District Second Precinct.

Chief Gong's Interrogation and Confessions: Upon receiving the report, Chief Gong Houzhai immediately ordered Officers Yuan and Lin, along with police chief Wang Shande and the entire police force, to rush to the scene. When the assistants from both sides saw the police arrive, they scattered like birds and beasts. The police arrested the group of people and the two live-ammunition handguns discarded on the ground and took them to the station. Yesterday, Chief Gong conducted a preliminary hearing. According to the plaintiff Chen Shiying, a 22-year-old man from Ningbo, Wang wanted to extort 50 yuan from him but failed, so he gathered bodyguard corps members to shoot at him. According to Wang, he went to Chen's house in his friend Wang Alin's car, and Chen shouted "kidnapping." He was informed by the bodyguard corps and taken to the Huaiyang Teahouse to "drink tea," so he instigated the corps members to open fire. Jiang Fuchun from Liuhe, 21 years old, Zhao Lianfa from Shanghai, 18 years old, Li Jinzhong from Yangzhou, 36 years old, Li Fucheng from Baoshan, 21 years old, and Dan Fengwu from Jiading, 30 years old, all said that they were members of the First Team and were ordered by Platoon Leader Luo to investigate the situation at the Huaiyang Teahouse and did not beat anyone. Xiao Wenbin from Yancheng, 21 years old, and Jin Xianglin from Shanghai, 23 years old, who were members of the Eighth Team of the Bodyguard Corps, also denied firing shots and fighting. Chief Gong reviewed the confessions and, considering the case involved a crowd gathering to open fire and fight, although no one was injured, it violated criminal law and ordered that they all be transferred to the bureau for further investigation. The confiscated car was claimed by its owner yesterday.

Old Clerk Reports Bizarre Robbery 129

Why Would Robbers Take a Big Roundabout Route?

Inconsistent and Incomplete Details Arousing Suspicion

Xie Sheng Fruit Shop, located opposite the Xiaodongmen Police Station in the French Concession, has been in business for many years and has always been very prosperous. The shop has an old clerk named Zhang Misheng, 39 years old, from Chuansha, who has been working there for more than twenty years. He is usually considered diligent and careful in his work. Yesterday morning around 9:00 AM, Zhang was ordered by the accountant to take 2,700 yuan in banknotes, 300 yuan in silver dollars, and three promissory notes totaling 460 yuan, placing them in a money-carrying bamboo basket, and send them to Deqin Xin Money Exchange in Langjiaqiao outside the Dadongmen in Nanshi for deposit. Unexpectedly, around 11:00 AM, Zhang suddenly went to the First District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau to report that he had encountered robbers on the road and all the banknotes had been stolen. When Officer Ren of the district conducted a preliminary hearing, Zhang Misheng stated, "Just now, I walked out of the shop and passed the back gate of the Jie Pufeng Guild Hall on Li Ma Road. Suddenly, four robbers wearing blue cloth long gowns and speaking with a northern accent ordered me to stop and immediately pulled out guns, forbidding me from making any noise. They hired three rickshaws, forced me to ride in one, and the other two were ridden by two robbers each. One robber walked in front, and one walked behind the rickshaw. My rickshaw was in the middle of the two rickshaws ridden by the robbers. I was escorted south to Yanmatou, passing through Yangjiadu Hengjie and Laobaidu Hengjie, then west through Longwangmiao, south along Doushi Street, turning to Zixia Road, then south through Wangjia Zuijiao, reaching Wangjia Wharf, west into Xiaojiuhua Street, then south along Zhonghua Road, until we reached the entrance of the Shanghai Social Bureau, where we finally stopped. The two robbers immediately came up and snatched the 2,700 yuan in banknotes, 300 yuan in silver dollars, and three promissory notes totaling 460 yuan from the basket I was carrying, taking the stolen goods and fleeing. The remaining two robbers then took me to Qiaojia Bang, turned into Yongxing Street, and arrived at Yujia Alley, where the two robbers finally fled in different directions. However, the 118 yuan in banknotes that I had on my person was not stolen. I immediately returned to the shop to report and then came here to report for investigation." The district officer found that the details stated by Zhang were not entirely true and that such a robbery was unheard of. How could there be such foolish robbers? When they encounter the victim, they should rob immediately to avoid failure. Why would they ride rickshaws in a big roundabout route until they reached the entrance of the Social Bureau on Zhonghua Road before taking action? Could that place be more conducive to robbing? Moreover, there were police officers from the Third Precinct of the First District stationed at the entrance of the Social Bureau, and across the street was the headquarters of the Shanghai South Bodyguard Corps, and nearby was the Xiaonanmen Outpost of the Third Precinct of the First District. How could the robbers be so bold as to rob on that road? Furthermore, Zhang did not report to the police on duty afterward, only coming to the district to report more than an hour later. All of this suggests that there is something hidden. He ordered a formal document to be prepared and Zhang Misheng to be sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for strict investigation to uncover the truth.

Local Area Heavy Fog Halts Over Forty Ocean-Going Vessels 130

In recent days, as the weather has warmed, heavy fog has occurred in this port and off the coast of Wusong. Shanghai's import and export merchant ships were halted by the fog yesterday, unable to enter the port, resulting in delays to scheduled services for dozens of vessels. Detailed information is as follows:

Ocean-Going Vessels Halted: North and South Seas coastal ships arriving in Shanghai yesterday from Shantou, Hong Kong, Guangzhou, Yantai, Tianjin, Qingdao, Dalian, etc., including the Taikoo Jardine's "Guangdong," "Ding Sheng," Nisshin's "Rojozan Maru," D汽's "Dalian Maru," etc., were all scheduled to enter the port yesterday. However, these ocean-going vessels encountered heavy fog the night before in the waters off Wusong. Due to the navigation routes on the sea being obscured by the fog, the ships were unable to proceed and dared not take the risk of causing accidents. They collectively anchored at sea to take shelter. However, the heavy fog did not dissipate throughout yesterday, preventing the ocean-going vessels from entering the port until late at night.

Mail Ships Delayed: The Pacific Line mail ship "President Coolidge" of the Dollar Line, arriving in Shanghai from Seattle, the Nippon Yusen Kaisha's European route mail ship "Suwa Maru," arriving in Shanghai from London, and the British company's "Nilanshi," also arriving in Shanghai from Europe, all scheduled to arrive in Shanghai yesterday, were also hindered by the heavy fog and were delayed. They may be able to enter the port today if the fog dissipates. Outbound mail ships, such as the "Taileer" of 美最時 and the "Dunkirk" of 大英, bound for Hamburg and London, arrived at the Wusongkou yesterday and are also waiting for the fog to clear before proceeding. Riverboats Not Arrived: In previous heavy fogs, Yangtze River boats have always entered the port without delay. However, this time the fog was particularly heavy, and all Yangtze River boats of 六公司 were blocked at the mouth of the Yangtze River, unable to sail to Shanghai, as there was also heavy fog in various parts of the Yangtze River. Not a single Yangtze River boat arrived yesterday, and only three merchant ships and one warship entered the port all day, causing all regular Yangtze River boats scheduled to depart this morning to be delayed.

All Ships Postponed: Yesterday, more than forty Jianghai vessels were blocked by fog outside the mouth of Wusong and unable to enter the port, which has affected the North and South Seas and Yangtze River schedules departing today. As usual, the ships "Tonghe," "Anqing," "Yisheng," "Jinan," "Nagasaki Maru," "Ikoma Maru," "Nilanya," "Mankok" and others scheduled to depart today have all postponed their departure dates due to the fog. This heavy fog has caused a "sea famine" in Shanghai, which is a rare occurrence. However, the Shanghai-Ningbo route liners "Xin Jiang Tian" and "Yong Xing" departed as usual.

Fang Jiaobo Discusses Various Types of Insurance 132

Fang Jiaobo, manager of the Shanghai General Insurance Office for Various Industries, spoke yesterday about various types of insurance, saying that insurance matters have always been controlled by foreign merchants, with Chinese merchants accounting for only one-tenth, and the outflow of profits being extremely small. The reason for this is that the majority of policyholders tend to favor foreign merchants, which is truly distressing. Recently, Chinese merchants' insurance is not without capacity. Colleagues in various industries believe that the fundamental interest of policyholders lies in the industries themselves, so they can shift their mentality and promote Chinese merchants' insurance, which will have a significant effect. At the same time, considering that policyholders have been oppressed for a long time, and their wishes are often violated when they suffer disasters, efforts should be made to alleviate their suffering. This led to the organization of the General Insurance Office for Various Industries, combining the strength of various industries, on the one hand, to promote the development of Chinese merchants' insurance industry, and on the other hand, to handle procedures on behalf of policyholders and safeguard their due rights. Since the beginning of the founding, colleagues have elected me as the general manager. I believe that this initiative is a social undertaking, not entirely a business nature, so I dare to take the task. I am willing to devote my meager efforts to serving the society as always and seek benefits for the public. Personally, I have only sacrifice and no rights. However, I know that my ability is weak, and I rely entirely on the support of all sectors of society to be successful.

International Charity Race Postponed to the 26th of This Month 133

The International Charity Race, originally scheduled for the 14th of this month, was suddenly postponed yesterday. A reporter from the Central News Agency inquired about the situation with the Finance Bureau. The person in charge of the bureau gave a detailed explanation, which is disclosed as follows: (1) From the date of initiation to the originally scheduled competition date, the time for handling the fundraising for the race was less than a month. Although it has received enthusiastic support from all sectors of society, the sales of lottery tickets have reached more than 85% (excluding the sales of the Jockey Club and foreign merchants, etc.), but there are many sales points in the various parks of the Municipal Council.

| Flowers Blooming Luxuriously in the Greenhouse of Zhaofeng Park | 134

In December of last year, Zhaofeng Park had a total of 30,275 visitors, Hongkou Park had 15,431 visitors, Waitan Park had 11,066 visitors, and Huishan, Sterly, Singapore, three parks, Nanyang Road, Yuyuan Road, Suzhou Road, and Kunshan Fangchang's various children's amusement parks had a total of 40,874 visitors. The flowers are blooming luxuriantly in the greenhouse of Zhaofeng Park. More than 40,000 spherical flower seeds have been planted in each park. The stronger annual flowers are being planted. Due to the sudden change in weather, it was postponed to February. All trees are being pruned in winter. Grass clumps have been erected in the flower beds to protect the more delicate seedlings from the cold. The Children's Playground on Difeng Road was closed on December 20th. The swings and other items, as well as most of the trees, have been moved to the Children's Amusement Park on Nanyang Road.

There are more than forty places, and the procedures for collecting ticket money, sorting out ticket stubs, and returning the remaining lottery tickets from a few sales points are extremely complicated. Even if the bureau sets a deadline, it is impossible to complete the matter in a few days. Moreover, this matter is co-organized by various Jockey Clubs, and many foreigners also support it. The bureau is responsible for promoting sales, and its responsibility is very heavy, and its reputation is at stake. It must handle the matters smoothly before holding the event. (2) The event is postponed to January 26th of this year, which is only twelve days from the original date, which is not too long. That day happens to be the Lunar New Year's Day. Shanghai society usually rests invisibly. The fundraising method for this race has been determined for the prize ticket commission, but the income from each race and ticket sales on that day, after expenses, is also fully allocated to relief efforts in disaster areas. Therefore, using that day can increase the audience, and the funds for disaster relief may be able to collect tens of thousands of dollars more. Based on these two reasons, the bureau and the Jockey Club both agreed to postpone the event. As for the ticket money, as of the 9th of this month, the bureau has transferred 755,000 yuan to the Shanghai Race Club, and the number deposited by the Race Club in HSBC is said to reach 830,000 yuan, which has exceeded the total amount of awards, etc. It is found that the last time this port held a horse race to raise money for the flood, the ticket money was not fully concluded until the day of the competition, resulting in a compromise method of competing before the conclusion. This time, the competition will be held at the Shanghai Race Club, which concerns the credibility of both Chinese and foreigners, so the Finance Bureau advocates concluding the matter properly in advance.

New Ferry Launched in the City

Extremely Convenient with Double-Ended Operation 135

The city-run ferry strives to be perfect in equipment such as ships and wharves, and the journey is safe, fast, and convenient for travelers. Since the opening of the Jiang Ferry, it has been open regardless of wind or rain, and the fees are particularly low. Although the business has losses, it is willing to take care of the livelihood of the common people. Recently, it was heard that two diesel-powered Jiang ferries operating on both ends are planned ( ), and the latest fish-backed steel rudder is used, which can rotate freely and is very effective. It can also carry two cars, and even freight cars can be carried because the roof of the ship is active and can be removed at any time. The ferry was launched at the He Xing Factory in Nanshi on the morning of the 8th of this month, and it will be completed soon. The purpose of operating on both ends is to avoid the cumbersome process of turning around and the danger of collision, which is unprecedented in the country. The fish-backed rudder blades are an original idea in Beijing. In the future, the official opening will benefit travelers.

Talk about Increasing the Price of City Ferries: Second Class Will Not Be Increased for the Time Being

Recently, the city's city ferry has increased the price of the special and first-class fares for the long ferry (Shanghai to Gaoqiao) due to increased costs and business losses. A reporter from the Central News Agency inquired with the ferry and was told that the ferry was originally set up to popularize civilian transportation, so the second-class cabin is the main body, and its special first-class passengers are mostly those who visit the suburbs in spring, summer, and autumn, while the second class is more prosperous in winter. Therefore, the special first class is mostly tourists, and the second class is ordinary passengers. This time the price increase will not be applied to the second class, no matter how expensive the materials are or how much the cost increases. However, in order to take care of the cost, we have to find other ways to remedy it, so we will increase the special first-class fare as appropriate to supplement it. The second class will still be charged at the old price more than ten years ago. Moreover, the city-run Jiang Ferry lines cost tens of thousands of yuan, and the fares charged are almost the same as those of private ferries with boats worth hundreds of yuan, resulting in huge losses. These passengers are all ordinary passengers, and the fares cannot be increased again, so the business losses cannot but be compensated by the long ferry tourists. In other words, I hope to make tourists with more financial resources increase their burden to make up for the business losses suffered by the second-class seats and the Jiang Ferry. The meaning is the same as that of various countries in Europe and the United States and this country imposing heavy taxes on luxury goods. Recently, the rear cabin of the first class has been removed to expand the second-class seats to avoid crowding.

With a Difference of One Thought, an Engineer Improperly Received 3,000 Yuan 137

A Money Shop Mistakenly Paid a Huge Amount

Duan Zhiyun Repeatedly Lied

| Stolen Evidence Seized, Fine of 400 Yuan | 138

Duan Zhiyun, a local construction engineer of the Yizhong Real Estate Company at No. 6 Jiujiang Road, took a bank draft for one hundred taels of silver to the Hengxiang Money Shop at No. 18 Ningbo Road in the morning before yesterday to exchange it for cash. At that time, a Mr. Wang also went to the shop to exchange money. Wang had business dealings with the shop, so he handed a bank draft for 3,000 yuan to the accountant and went to another room to visit a friend. Later, Shao Yaochen, the accountant of the shop, handed 3,000 yuan in banknotes to Shao Zhenxiang, a shop clerk, for transfer. Because Mr. Wang was not seen, and only Duan Zhiyun was waiting outside the counter to receive the money, Zhenxiang mistakenly identified Duan as the person who wanted to receive the 3,000 yuan and paid it to him. Although Duan knew it was a mistake, he was temporarily blinded by greed and took the money and left. After Duan left, Shao Yaochen suddenly became suspicious and realized the mistake after checking. He rushed out to chase him, but he had lost track of the person who took the money. He took Duan's bank draft for one hundred taels of silver to the General Patrol Room to report and requested an investigation. The head detective found that the one hundred tael ticket was issued by the Huacheng Canvas Factory, and Duan Zhiyun's seal was stamped on the back of the ticket. He sent detective Ma Mouxiang and a Western detective to Huacheng to investigate and found out where Duan worked. He went to Yizhong Company to inquire and was told that Duan had returned to his residence at No. 1 Minxin Lane, Mintini Yin Road, French Concession. The Chinese and Western detectives rushed to Duan's house, but Duan not only denied taking the 3,000 yuan, but also denied his original name, saying that his name was Wang Zhenxiang. However, Shao Zhenxiang, a shop clerk of Hengxiang who went with the detectives, still recognized this face and insisted that the money was indeed paid to this person. The detectives then began to search and found 45 yuan in banknotes in Duan's pocket and 120 yuan in his trouser legs. Shao Zhenxiang identified all of these banknotes as being paid by the shop. The green tickets were stamped with the word "Xin," which was easy to identify. However, Duan still did not directly admit it, claiming that it was exchanged for a one-hundred-tael silver ticket, but the amount did not match. Therefore, the detectives took Duan and the banknotes to the patrol room and investigated the remaining money. Until 1:30 am yesterday morning, the Chinese and Western detectives went to Duan's house again to search and found 2,800 yuan in banknotes under the table in the kitchen. Together with the money found on Duan, only 35 yuan was missing. At this point, Duan also admitted that he had spent the missing 35 yuan because the stolen evidence was all there and he could not deny it. At 9:00, the two Shaos of Hengxiang were summoned and Duan and the stolen money were taken to the First Special District Local Court. Judge Liu Yugui interrogated him. After the patrol room lawyer Qian Xunjiu stated the case, he requested strict punishment because the defendant had intentionally embezzled other people's property. Judge Liu then clearly questioned all the witnesses and sentenced Duan Zhiyun to a fine of 400 yuan. If he was unable to pay, he would be allowed to offset it with one day of imprisonment for every three yuan. The seized banknotes were handed over to the original owner for collection, and the insufficient amount was deducted from Duan Zhiyun's original one hundred tael money. After the judgment, Duan stated that he would appeal, so he was ordered to pay 400 yuan for bail pending review during the appeal period.

Inauguration Meeting of the Industrial and Commercial Progressive Society 141

▲ Elected 15 Directors and 7 Alternate Directors

▲Telegraphed and Encouraged North China Generals to Unite in the War of Resistance Against Japan

The Shanghai Industrial and Commercial Progressive Society held its inaugural meeting at the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA yesterday. More than 100 people, including Shen Weiting, Chen Xikang, Gu Huimin, and Ding Jinsheng, attended. He Yuanming, Sun Mingqi, and Zhang Dafu were publicly elected as the presidium. After performing the ceremony as scheduled, the chairman first reported the purpose of the meeting, and then the preparatory member reported the preparations. Then, the articles of association were discussed and directors were elected. As a result, He Yuanming, Sun Mingqi, Zhao Erchang, Mao Yun, Zhang Dafu, Jin Chuxiang, Wang Manyun, Xu Chao, Cheng Yujie, Fu Keming, Yuan Mingjun, Qiu Liangyu, Xue Guangqian, Cai Xiaohe, and Chen Liangyu were elected as directors. Hu Shouqi, Shen Weiting, Yu Tang, Chu Yumin, Li Ruzhang, Wang Honghui, and Lin Guyun were elected as alternate directors. After the election, the following proposals were discussed: (1) The proposal to set up a Chinese Industrial and Commercial Bank to enrich the foundation of the Society was decided to be approved in principle. The detailed plan and specific plan will be drafted by the original proposer and handed over to the Board of Directors for processing. (2) The proposal to lease the Society's site was decided that the site will be leased by the Board of Directors, but the lease fee is limited to 50 yuan per month. (3) The proposal on how the Society should express its views on the invasion of North China by the Japanese invaders was decided that the General Assembly will issue a telegram to encourage the generals of North China to unite in the war of resistance against Japan. (4) The proposal to register with party and government agencies was decided to be handed over to the Board of Directors for processing. (5) The proposal on whether the surplus of the dinner fee should be subsidized to the Society's expenses was decided that the fees for all absences and leaves of absence from the first time will be calculated to subsidize the Society's expenses. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

A Young Woman Swallows Tranquilizer Pills Due to Unfreedom in Marriage

| Life in Danger | 147

Shen Dongfu, the owner of the Linchenxiang Paint Store on Xingsheng Street in the French Concession, is about 40 years old and lives at Number 23 Renjili, Dengtuo Road, Hongkou. He has only one daughter, named Meiyun, who is 28 years old and unmarried. She is beautiful, educated, and has modern ideas. Recently, a friend of her father's came to act as a matchmaker. The proposed family is an old-fashioned family, and her mother has already agreed. Meiyun heard this and strongly disagreed, because it concerned her lifelong happiness and she could not consent. In her anger, she attempted suicide by secretly taking six tranquilizer pills with brandy yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM. Soon, the poison took effect, and her condition became critical. She was discovered and taken to Tongren Hospital, and then transferred to Guangren Hospital for treatment. It is reported that her condition is very critical.

Compilation and Publication of Trademark Bureau's Trademark Compendium

First Edition of East Asia Section to Be Distributed to All Sectors 148

He Zhuoxian, Director of the Trademark Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, recently recognized the importance of promoting domestic goods. However, people often find it difficult to distinguish between domestic and foreign goods in the market due to the vast variety of products. Therefore, he has undertaken a very important task: compiling a "Trademark Compendium" that includes trademarks from various countries, divided into two major sections: East Asia and Europe, America, Africa, etc. The printing costs alone will be tens of thousands of dollars, indicating its meticulousness. The plan is to first publish the East Asia section of the Trademark Compendium. Director He and his colleagues are working day and night to complete it. It is expected to be finished in about a month. After publication, it will be distributed to all sectors so that everyone can have a copy and be able to identify goods based on the illustrations, avoiding confusion and making it easier to investigate. This is truly a significant new contribution to the promotion of domestic goods this year.

Boy Dies After Being Run Over by Car While Crossing the Street 149

An elderly local woman, Xu Tao, who lives at Number 41 Masnan Road in the French Concession, was leading her three grandchildren, carrying one in her arms and leading two others, on the morning of the 9th of this month at 11:15 AM. They were walking westward at the intersection of Huanlong Road and Masnan Road. At that time, her five-year-old grandson, Gui Fu, was walking alone on the south side of the road, while the elderly woman and the others were walking on the north side. As they approached the Masnan Road intersection, Gui Fu suddenly crossed the road, running from south to north towards his grandmother. As he reached the middle of the road, a sedan driven by Shen Er, chauffeur to a certain Englishman with license plate number 7958, was traveling north on Masnan Road and turning west onto Huanlong Road. The car was unable to avoid the child and knocked him down, injuring his head and causing bleeding from his ears, rendering him unconscious. The police arrived and took the injured child to Guangci Hospital for treatment, and took the driver to the police station to report to the head officer for investigation. The child's brain injuries were too severe, and he died shortly after being admitted to the hospital. The hospital notified the police station, and the body was taken to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home for an autopsy. Yesterday morning, the Transportation Department requested Deng Baosun, the prosecutor from the Second Special District Court, to come to the funeral home to examine the body. After the autopsy, he held a hearing to question the defendant and the grandmother of the deceased regarding the incident. He concluded that Xu Gui Fu had died from a head injury caused by being hit by a car. The body was released to the family, Xu Tao, after they signed a guarantee. The defendant was returned to the Transportation Department for legal proceedings.

Letter to the Editor 157

To the esteemed editor of the Shen Bao: I was shocked and dismayed to read the news item "Landlord Beats Tenant Over Rent" in your local news column on January 9, 1933. Our agency, which manages the rental property, has found that the tenant in Sanxin Lane, citing losses from the war, has been deliberately defaulting on rent for nine months (from May 1932 to January 1933, a total of nine months). Prior to May 1932, we had already exempted three months' rent in accordance with the municipal government's order. Despite our agency's kind persuasion and patience, we were unsuccessful. On the 6th of this month, because the rent collector insisted on collecting the rent, he provoked the anger of Dr. Jiao Fuyin and his wife, the tenants, leading to a conflict. The rent collector's friend saw the injustice and provided assistance, resulting in a mutual scuffle. The facts are all there, and police officers from the First Precinct of the Fifth District were present as witnesses. The report in your newspaper that "the landlord suddenly gathered more than ten people to beat the doctor and his wife severely, destroyed their belongings, and stole their clothes, etc." is completely untrue. We respectfully request that your newspaper correct this report. Sincerely, Chen Qun, lawyer, January 10.
